 9991 // String equals
 9992 instruct string_equalsL(iRegP str1, iRegP str2, iRegI cnt, iRegI result, roddRegL oddReg, revenRegL evenReg, flagsReg cr) %{
 9993   match(Set result (StrEquals (Binary str1 str2) cnt));
 9994   effect(TEMP oddReg, TEMP evenReg, KILL cr); // R0, R1 are killed, too.
 9995   predicate(((StrEqualsNode*)n)->encoding() == StrIntrinsicNode::LL);
 9996   ins_cost(300);
 9997   format %{ "String Equals byte[] $str1,$str2,$cnt -> $result" %}
 9998   ins_encode %{
 9999     __ array_equals(false, $str1$$Register, $str2$$Register,
10000                     $cnt$$Register, $oddReg$$Register, $evenReg$$Register,
10001                     $result$$Register, true /* byte */);
10002   %}
10003   ins_pipe(pipe_class_dummy);
10004 %}
10005 
10006 instruct string_equalsU(iRegP str1, iRegP str2, iRegI cnt, iRegI result, roddRegL oddReg, revenRegL evenReg, flagsReg cr) %{
10007   match(Set result (StrEquals (Binary str1 str2) cnt));
10008   effect(TEMP oddReg, TEMP evenReg, KILL cr); // R0, R1 are killed, too.
10009   predicate(((StrEqualsNode*)n)->encoding() == StrIntrinsicNode::UU || ((StrEqualsNode*)n)->encoding() == StrIntrinsicNode::none);
10010   ins_cost(300);
10011   format %{ "String Equals char[] $str1,$str2,$cnt -> $result" %}
10012   ins_encode %{
10013     __ array_equals(false, $str1$$Register, $str2$$Register,
10014                     $cnt$$Register, $oddReg$$Register, $evenReg$$Register,
10015                     $result$$Register, false /* byte */);
10016   %}
10017   ins_pipe(pipe_class_dummy);
10018 %}
10019 
10020 instruct string_equals_imm(iRegP str1, iRegP str2, uimmI8 cnt, iRegI result, flagsReg cr) %{
10021   match(Set result (StrEquals (Binary str1 str2) cnt));
10022   effect(KILL cr); // R0 is killed, too.
10023   predicate(((StrEqualsNode*)n)->encoding() == StrIntrinsicNode::LL || ((StrEqualsNode*)n)->encoding() == StrIntrinsicNode::UU);
10024   ins_cost(100);
10025   format %{ "String Equals byte[] $str1,$str2,$cnt -> $result" %}
10026   ins_encode %{
10027     const int cnt_imm = $cnt$$constant;
10028     if (cnt_imm) { __ z_clc(0, cnt_imm - 1, $str1$$Register, 0, $str2$$Register); }
10029     __ z_lhi($result$$Register, 1);
10030     if (cnt_imm) {
10031       if (VM_Version::has_LoadStoreConditional()) {
10032         __ z_lhi(Z_R0_scratch, 0);
10033         __ z_locr($result$$Register, Z_R0_scratch, Assembler::bcondNotEqual);
10034       } else {
10035         Label Lskip;
10036         __ z_bre(Lskip);
10037         __ clear_reg($result$$Register);
10038         __ bind(Lskip);
10039       }
10040     }
10041   %}
10042   ins_pipe(pipe_class_dummy);
10043 %}
10044 
10045 instruct string_equalsC_imm(iRegP str1, iRegP str2, immI8 cnt, iRegI result, flagsReg cr) %{
10046   match(Set result (StrEquals (Binary str1 str2) cnt));
10047   effect(KILL cr); // R0 is killed, too.
10048   predicate(((StrEqualsNode*)n)->encoding() == StrIntrinsicNode::none);
10049   ins_cost(100);
10050   format %{ "String Equals $str1,$str2,$cnt -> $result" %}
10051   ins_encode %{
10052     const int cnt_imm = $cnt$$constant; // positive immI8 (7 bits used)
10053     if (cnt_imm) { __ z_clc(0, (cnt_imm << 1) - 1, $str1$$Register, 0, $str2$$Register); }
10054     __ z_lhi($result$$Register, 1);
10055     if (cnt_imm) {
10056       if (VM_Version::has_LoadStoreConditional()) {
10057         __ z_lhi(Z_R0_scratch, 0);
10058         __ z_locr($result$$Register, Z_R0_scratch, Assembler::bcondNotEqual);
10059       } else {
10060         Label Lskip;
10061         __ z_bre(Lskip);
10062         __ clear_reg($result$$Register);
10063         __ bind(Lskip);
10064       }
10065     }
10066   %}
10067   ins_pipe(pipe_class_dummy);
10068 %}

10175 instruct indexOf_imm1_U(iRegP haystack, iRegI haycnt, immP needle, immI_1 needlecnt, iRegI result, roddRegL oddReg, revenRegL evenReg, flagsReg cr) %{
10176   match(Set result (StrIndexOf (Binary haystack haycnt) (Binary needle needlecnt)));
10177   effect(TEMP_DEF result, TEMP evenReg, TEMP oddReg, KILL cr); // R0, R1 are killed, too.
10178   predicate(((StrIndexOfNode*)n)->encoding() == StrIntrinsicNode::UU || ((StrIndexOfNode*)n)->encoding() == StrIntrinsicNode::none);
10179   ins_cost(200);
10180   format %{ "String IndexOf UL [0..$haycnt]($haystack), [0]($needle) -> $result" %}

10185     jchar chr;
10186 #ifdef VM_LITTLE_ENDIAN
10187     Unimplemented();
10188 #else
10189     chr = (((jchar)(unsigned char)needle_values->element_value(0).as_byte()) << 8) |
10190            ((jchar)(unsigned char)needle_values->element_value(1).as_byte());
10191 #endif
10192     __ string_indexof_char($result$$Register,
10193                            $haystack$$Register, $haycnt$$Register,

10406 //----------PEEPHOLE RULES-----------------------------------------------------
10407 // These must follow all instruction definitions as they use the names
10408 // defined in the instructions definitions.
10409 //
10410 // peepmatch (root_instr_name [preceeding_instruction]*);
10411 //
10412 // peepconstraint %{
10413 // (instruction_number.operand_name relational_op instruction_number.operand_name
10414 //  [, ...]);
10415 // // instruction numbers are zero-based using left to right order in peepmatch
10416 //
10417 // peepreplace (instr_name([instruction_number.operand_name]*));
10418 // // provide an instruction_number.operand_name for each operand that appears
10419 // // in the replacement instruction's match rule
10420 //
10421 // ---------VM FLAGS---------------------------------------------------------
10422 //
10423 // All peephole optimizations can be turned off using -XX:-OptoPeephole
10424 //
10425 // Each peephole rule is given an identifying number starting with zero and
10426 // increasing by one in the order seen by the parser. An individual peephole
10427 // can be enabled, and all others disabled, by using -XX:OptoPeepholeAt=#
10428 // on the command-line.
10429 //
10430 // ---------CURRENT LIMITATIONS----------------------------------------------
10431 //
10432 // Only match adjacent instructions in same basic block
10433 // Only equality constraints
10434 // Only constraints between operands, not (0.dest_reg == EAX_enc)
10435 // Only one replacement instruction
10436 //
10437 // ---------EXAMPLE----------------------------------------------------------
10438 //
10439 // // pertinent parts of existing instructions in architecture description
10440 // instruct movI(eRegI dst, eRegI src) %{
10441 //   match(Set dst (CopyI src));
10442 // %}
10443 //
10444 // instruct incI_eReg(eRegI dst, immI1 src, eFlagsReg cr) %{
10445 //   match(Set dst (AddI dst src));
10446 //   effect(KILL cr);
10447 // %}
10448 //
10449 // // Change (inc mov) to lea
10450 // peephole %{
10451 //   // increment preceeded by register-register move
10452 //   peepmatch (incI_eReg movI);
10453 //   // require that the destination register of the increment
10454 //   // match the destination register of the move
10455 //   peepconstraint (0.dst == 1.dst);
10456 //   // construct a replacement instruction that sets
10457 //   // the destination to (move's source register + one)
10458 //   peepreplace (leaI_eReg_immI(0.dst 1.src 0.src));
10459 // %}
10460 //
10461 // Implementation no longer uses movX instructions since
10462 // machine-independent system no longer uses CopyX nodes.
10463 //
10464 // peephole %{
10465 //   peepmatch (incI_eReg movI);
10466 //   peepconstraint (0.dst == 1.dst);
10467 //   peepreplace (leaI_eReg_immI(0.dst 1.src 0.src));
10468 // %}
10469 //
10470 // peephole %{
10471 //   peepmatch (decI_eReg movI);
10472 //   peepconstraint (0.dst == 1.dst);
10473 //   peepreplace (leaI_eReg_immI(0.dst 1.src 0.src));
10474 // %}
10475 //
10476 // peephole %{
10477 //   peepmatch (addI_eReg_imm movI);
10478 //   peepconstraint (0.dst == 1.dst);
10479 //   peepreplace (leaI_eReg_immI(0.dst 1.src 0.src));
10480 // %}
10481 //
10482 // peephole %{
10483 //   peepmatch (addP_eReg_imm movP);
10484 //   peepconstraint (0.dst == 1.dst);
10485 //   peepreplace (leaP_eReg_immI(0.dst 1.src 0.src));
10486 // %}
10487 
10488 
10489 //  This peephole rule does not work, probably because ADLC can't handle two effects:
10490 //  Effect 1 is defining 0.op1 and effect 2 is setting CC
10491 // condense a load from memory and subsequent test for zero
10492 // into a single, more efficient ICM instruction.
10493 // peephole %{
10494 //   peepmatch (compI_iReg_imm0 loadI);
10495 //   peepconstraint (1.dst == 0.op1);
10496 //   peepreplace (loadtest15_iReg_mem(0.op1 0.op1 1.mem));
10497 // %}
10498 
10499 // // Change load of spilled value to only a spill
10500 // instruct storeI(memory mem, eRegI src) %{
10501 //   match(Set mem (StoreI mem src));
10502 // %}
10503 //
10504 // instruct loadI(eRegI dst, memory mem) %{
10505 //   match(Set dst (LoadI mem));
10506 // %}
10507 //
10508 peephole %{
10509   peepmatch (loadI storeI);
10510   peepconstraint (1.src == 0.dst, 1.mem == 0.mem);
10511   peepreplace (storeI(1.mem 1.mem 1.src));
10512 %}
10513 
10514 peephole %{
10515   peepmatch (loadL storeL);
10516   peepconstraint (1.src == 0.dst, 1.mem == 0.mem);
10517   peepreplace (storeL(1.mem 1.mem 1.src));
10518 %}
10519 
10520 peephole %{
10521   peepmatch (loadP storeP);
10522   peepconstraint (1.src == 0.dst, 1.dst == 0.mem);
10523   peepreplace (storeP(1.dst 1.dst 1.src));
10524 %}

10535   // TODO: s390 port size(FIXED_SIZE);
10536   format %{ "STE      $src,$mem\t # replicate(float2stack)" %}
10537   opcode(STE_ZOPC, STE_ZOPC);
10538   ins_encode(z_form_rt_mem(src, mem));
10539   ins_pipe(pipe_class_dummy);

10554 // Replicate scalar int to packed int values (8 Bytes)
10555 instruct expand_Repl2I_reg(iRegL dst, iRegL src) %{
10556   // Dummy match rule, false predicate, for expand only.
10557   match(Set dst (ConvI2L src));
10558   predicate(false);
10559   ins_cost(DEFAULT_COST);
10560   // TODO: s390 port size(FIXED_SIZE);
10561   format %{ "REPLIC2F $dst,$src\t # replicate(pack2F)" %}
10562   ins_encode %{
10563     if ($dst$$Register == $src$$Register) {
10564       __ z_sllg(Z_R0_scratch, $src$$Register, 64-32);
10565       __ z_ogr($dst$$Register, Z_R0_scratch);
10566     }  else {
10567       __ z_sllg($dst$$Register, $src$$Register, 64-32);
10568       __ z_ogr( $dst$$Register, $src$$Register);
10569     }
10570   %}
10571   ins_pipe(pipe_class_dummy);
10572 %}

10760   format %{ "REPLIC2F $dst,$src\t # pack2F direct" %}
10761   ins_encode %{
10762     assert(VM_Version::has_FPSupportEnhancements(), "encoder should never be called on old H/W");
10763     __ z_lgdr($dst$$Register, $src$$FloatRegister);
10764 
10765     __ z_srlg(Z_R0_scratch, $dst$$Register, 32);  // Floats are left-justified in 64bit reg.
10766     __ z_iilf($dst$$Register, 0);                 // Save a "result not ready" stall.
10767     __ z_ogr($dst$$Register, Z_R0_scratch);
10768   %}
10769   ins_pipe(pipe_class_dummy);
10770 %}
10771 
10772 // Replicate scalar float immediate to packed float values in GREG (8 Bytes).
10773 instruct Repl2F_imm(iRegL dst, immF src) %{
10774   match(Set dst (ReplicateF src));
10775   predicate(n->as_Vector()->length() == 2);
10776   ins_should_rematerialize(true);
10777   format %{ "REPLIC2F $dst,$src\t # pack2F imm" %}
10778   ins_encode %{
10779     union {
10780       int   Isrc32;
10781       float Fsrc32;
10782     };
10783     Fsrc32 = $src$$constant;
10784     __ z_llilf($dst$$Register, Isrc32);
10785     __ z_iihf($dst$$Register, Isrc32);
10786   %}
10787   ins_pipe(pipe_class_dummy);
10788 %}
10789 
10790 // Replicate scalar float immediate zeroes to packed float values in GREG (8 Bytes).
10791 // Do this only for 'real' zeroes, especially don't loose sign of negative zeroes.
10792 instruct Repl2F_imm0(iRegL dst, immFp0 src) %{
10793   match(Set dst (ReplicateF src));
10794   predicate(n->as_Vector()->length() == 2);
10795   ins_should_rematerialize(true);
10796   format %{ "REPLIC2F $dst,$src\t # pack2F imm0" %}
10797   ins_encode %{ __ z_laz($dst$$Register, 0, Z_R0); %}
10798   ins_pipe(pipe_class_dummy);
10799 %}

10846   ins_cost(DEFAULT_COST);
10847   // TODO: s390 port size(FIXED_SIZE);
10848   format %{ "LRVGR   $dst,$src\t # byte reverse long" %}
10849   opcode(LRVGR_ZOPC);
10850   ins_encode(z_rreform(dst, src));
10851   ins_pipe(pipe_class_dummy);
10852 %}
10853 
10854 // Leading zeroes
10855 
10856 // The instruction FLOGR (Find Leftmost One in Grande (64bit) Register)
10857 // returns the bit position of the leftmost 1 in the 64bit source register.
10858 // As the bits are numbered from left to right (0..63), the returned
10859 // position index is equivalent to the number of leading zeroes.
10860 // If no 1-bit is found (i.e. the regsiter contains zero), the instruction
10861 // returns position 64. That's exactly what we need.
10862 
10863 instruct countLeadingZerosI(revenRegI dst, iRegI src, roddRegI tmp, flagsReg cr) %{
10864   match(Set dst (CountLeadingZerosI src));
10865   effect(KILL tmp, KILL cr);
10866   ins_cost(3 * DEFAULT_COST);
10867   size(14);
10868   format %{ "SLLG    $dst,$src,32\t # no need to always count 32 zeroes first\n\t"
10869             "IILH    $dst,0x8000 \t # insert \"stop bit\" to force result 32 for zero src.\n\t"
10870             "FLOGR   $dst,$dst"
10871          %}
10872   ins_encode %{
10873     // Performance experiments indicate that "FLOGR" is using some kind of
10874     // iteration to find the leftmost "1" bit.
10875     //
10876     // The prior implementation zero-extended the 32-bit argument to 64 bit,
10877     // thus forcing "FLOGR" to count 32 bits of which we know they are zero.
10878     // We could gain measurable speedup in micro benchmark:
10879     //
10880     //               leading   trailing
10881     //   z10:   int     2.04       1.68
10882     //         long     1.00       1.02
10883     //   z196:  int     0.99       1.23
10884     //         long     1.00       1.11
10885     //
10886     // By shifting the argument into the high-word instead of zero-extending it.
10887     // The add'l branch on condition (taken for a zero argument, very infrequent,
10888     // good prediction) is well compensated for by the savings.
10889     //
10890     // We leave the previous implementation in for some time in the future when
10891     // the "FLOGR" instruction may become less iterative.
10892 
10893     // Version 2: shows 62%(z9), 204%(z10), -1%(z196) improvement over original
10894     __ z_sllg($dst$$Register, $src$$Register, 32); // No need to always count 32 zeroes first.
10895     __ z_iilh($dst$$Register, 0x8000);   // Insert "stop bit" to force result 32 for zero src.
10896     __ z_flogr($dst$$Register, $dst$$Register);
10897   %}
10898   ins_pipe(pipe_class_dummy);
10899 %}
10900 
10901 instruct countLeadingZerosL(revenRegI dst, iRegL src, roddRegI tmp, flagsReg cr) %{
10902   match(Set dst (CountLeadingZerosL src));
10903   effect(KILL tmp, KILL cr);
10904   ins_cost(DEFAULT_COST);
10905   size(4);
10906   format %{ "FLOGR   $dst,$src \t # count leading zeros (long)\n\t" %}
10907   ins_encode %{ __ z_flogr($dst$$Register, $src$$Register); %}
10908   ins_pipe(pipe_class_dummy);
10909 %}
10910 
10911 // trailing zeroes
10912 
10913 // We transform the trailing zeroes problem to a leading zeroes problem
10914 // such that can use the FLOGR instruction to our advantage.
10915 
10916 // With
10917 //   tmp1 = src - 1
10918 // we flip all trailing zeroes to ones and the rightmost one to zero.
10919 // All other bits remain unchanged.
10920 // With the complement
10921 //   tmp2 = ~src
10922 // we get all ones in the trailing zeroes positions. Thus,
10923 //   tmp3 = tmp1 & tmp2
10924 // yields ones in the trailing zeroes positions and zeroes elsewhere.
10925 // Now we can apply FLOGR and get 64-(trailing zeroes).
10926 instruct countTrailingZerosI(revenRegI dst, iRegI src, roddRegI tmp, flagsReg cr) %{
10927   match(Set dst (CountTrailingZerosI src));
10928   effect(TEMP_DEF dst, TEMP tmp, KILL cr);
10929   ins_cost(8 * DEFAULT_COST);
10930   // TODO: s390 port size(FIXED_SIZE);  // Emitted code depends on PreferLAoverADD being on/off.
10931   format %{ "LLGFR   $dst,$src  \t # clear upper 32 bits (we are dealing with int)\n\t"
10932             "LCGFR   $tmp,$src  \t # load 2's complement (32->64 bit)\n\t"
10933             "AGHI    $dst,-1    \t # tmp1 = src-1\n\t"
10934             "AGHI    $tmp,-1    \t # tmp2 = -src-1 = ~src\n\t"
10935             "NGR     $dst,$tmp  \t # tmp3 = tmp1&tmp2\n\t"
10936             "FLOGR   $dst,$dst  \t # count trailing zeros (int)\n\t"
10937             "AHI     $dst,-64   \t # tmp4 = 64-(trailing zeroes)-64\n\t"
10938             "LCR     $dst,$dst  \t # res = -tmp4"
10939          %}
10940   ins_encode %{
10941     Register Rdst = $dst$$Register;
10942     Register Rsrc = $src$$Register;
10943     // Rtmp only needed for for zero-argument shortcut. With kill effect in
10944     // match rule Rsrc = roddReg would be possible, saving one register.
10945     Register Rtmp = $tmp$$Register;
10946 
10947     assert_different_registers(Rdst, Rsrc, Rtmp);
10948 
10949     // Algorithm:
10950     // - Isolate the least significant (rightmost) set bit using (src & (-src)).
10951     //   All other bits in the result are zero.
10952     // - Find the "leftmost one" bit position in the single-bit result from previous step.
10953     // - 63-("leftmost one" bit position) gives the # of trailing zeros.
10954 
10955     // Version 2: shows 79%(z9), 68%(z10), 23%(z196) improvement over original.
10956     Label done;
10957     __ load_const_optimized(Rdst, 32); // Prepare for shortcut (zero argument), result will be 32.
10958     __ z_lcgfr(Rtmp, Rsrc);
10959     __ z_bre(done);                    // Taken very infrequently, good prediction, no BHT entry.
10960 
10961     __ z_nr(Rtmp, Rsrc);               // (src) & (-src) leaves nothing but least significant bit.
10962     __ z_ahi(Rtmp,  -1);               // Subtract one to fill all trailing zero positions with ones.
10963                                        // Use 32bit op to prevent borrow propagation (case Rdst = 0x80000000)
10964                                        // into upper half of reg. Not relevant with sllg below.
10965     __ z_sllg(Rdst, Rtmp, 32);         // Shift interesting contents to upper half of register.
10966     __ z_bre(done);                    // Shortcut for argument = 1, result will be 0.
10967                                        // Depends on CC set by ahi above.
10968                                        // Taken very infrequently, good prediction, no BHT entry.
10969                                        // Branch delayed to have Rdst set correctly (Rtmp == 0(32bit)
10970                                        // after SLLG Rdst == 0(64bit)).
10971     __ z_flogr(Rdst, Rdst);            // Kills tmp which is the oddReg for dst.
10972     __ add2reg(Rdst,  -32);            // 32-pos(leftmost1) is #trailing zeros
10973     __ z_lcgfr(Rdst, Rdst);            // Provide 64bit result at no cost.
10974     __ bind(done);
10975   %}
10976   ins_pipe(pipe_class_dummy);
10977 %}
10978 
10979 instruct countTrailingZerosL(revenRegI dst, iRegL src, roddRegL tmp, flagsReg cr) %{
10980   match(Set dst (CountTrailingZerosL src));
10981   effect(TEMP_DEF dst, KILL tmp, KILL cr);
10982   ins_cost(8 * DEFAULT_COST);
10983   // TODO: s390 port size(FIXED_SIZE);  // Emitted code depends on PreferLAoverADD being on/off.
10984   format %{ "LCGR    $dst,$src  \t # preserve src\n\t"
10985             "NGR     $dst,$src  \t #\n\t"
10986             "AGHI    $dst,-1    \t # tmp1 = src-1\n\t"
10987             "FLOGR   $dst,$dst  \t # count trailing zeros (long), kill $tmp\n\t"
10988             "AHI     $dst,-64   \t # tmp4 = 64-(trailing zeroes)-64\n\t"
10989             "LCR     $dst,$dst  \t #"
10990          %}
10991   ins_encode %{
10992     Register Rdst = $dst$$Register;
10993     Register Rsrc = $src$$Register;
10994     assert_different_registers(Rdst, Rsrc); // Rtmp == Rsrc allowed.
10995 
10996     // New version: shows 5%(z9), 2%(z10), 11%(z196) improvement over original.
10997     __ z_lcgr(Rdst, Rsrc);
10998     __ z_ngr(Rdst, Rsrc);
10999     __ add2reg(Rdst,   -1);
11000     __ z_flogr(Rdst, Rdst); // Kills tmp which is the oddReg for dst.
11001     __ add2reg(Rdst,  -64);
11002     __ z_lcgfr(Rdst, Rdst); // Provide 64bit result at no cost.
11003   %}
11004   ins_pipe(pipe_class_dummy);
11005 %}
11006 
11007 
11008 // bit count
11009 
11010 instruct popCountI(iRegI dst, iRegI src, iRegI tmp, flagsReg cr) %{
11011   match(Set dst (PopCountI src));
11012   effect(TEMP_DEF dst, TEMP tmp, KILL cr);
11013   predicate(UsePopCountInstruction && VM_Version::has_PopCount());
11014   ins_cost(DEFAULT_COST);
11015   size(24);
11016   format %{ "POPCNT  $dst,$src\t # pop count int" %}
11017   ins_encode %{
11018     Register Rdst = $dst$$Register;
11019     Register Rsrc = $src$$Register;
11020     Register Rtmp = $tmp$$Register;
11021 
11022     // Prefer compile-time assertion over run-time SIGILL.
11023     assert(VM_Version::has_PopCount(), "bad predicate for countLeadingZerosI");
11024     assert_different_registers(Rdst, Rtmp);
11025 
11026     // Version 2: shows 10%(z196) improvement over original.
11027     __ z_popcnt(Rdst, Rsrc);
11028     __ z_srlg(Rtmp, Rdst, 16); // calc  byte4+byte6 and byte5+byte7
11029     __ z_alr(Rdst, Rtmp);      //   into byte6 and byte7
11030     __ z_srlg(Rtmp, Rdst,  8); // calc (byte4+byte6) + (byte5+byte7)
11031     __ z_alr(Rdst, Rtmp);      //   into byte7
11032     __ z_llgcr(Rdst, Rdst);    // zero-extend sum
11033   %}
11034   ins_pipe(pipe_class_dummy);
11035 %}
11036 
11037 instruct popCountL(iRegI dst, iRegL src, iRegL tmp, flagsReg cr) %{
11038   match(Set dst (PopCountL src));
11039   effect(TEMP_DEF dst, TEMP tmp, KILL cr);
11040   predicate(UsePopCountInstruction && VM_Version::has_PopCount());
11041   ins_cost(DEFAULT_COST);
11042   // TODO: s390 port size(FIXED_SIZE);
11043   format %{ "POPCNT  $dst,$src\t # pop count long" %}
11044   ins_encode %{
11045     Register Rdst = $dst$$Register;
11046     Register Rsrc = $src$$Register;
11047     Register Rtmp = $tmp$$Register;
11048 
11049     // Prefer compile-time assertion over run-time SIGILL.
11050     assert(VM_Version::has_PopCount(), "bad predicate for countLeadingZerosI");
11051     assert_different_registers(Rdst, Rtmp);
11052 
11053     // Original version. Using LA instead of algr seems to be a really bad idea (-35%).
11054     __ z_popcnt(Rdst, Rsrc);
11055     __ z_ahhlr(Rdst, Rdst, Rdst);
11056     __ z_sllg(Rtmp, Rdst, 16);
11057     __ z_algr(Rdst, Rtmp);
11058     __ z_sllg(Rtmp, Rdst,  8);
11059     __ z_algr(Rdst, Rtmp);
11060     __ z_srlg(Rdst, Rdst, 56);
11061   %}
11062   ins_pipe(pipe_class_dummy);
11063 %}
